# Fuzzing Triage Report

## Crash analysis
No crash was observed, attributable to four compounding factors grounded in the provided data. First, the beacon frame family is entirely absent: the AP's most-exercised inbound IE parser — the one that processes Beacon and Probe Response frames for clients and, by symmetry, any vendor-specific beacon-like injection path — was never stressed. Second, the 20 unique frames were replayed ~389 times each without variation; repetition of already-surviving frames cannot uncover new crashes, so the large frame count is misleading. Third, the oversized_value mutation inflates frame length but does not set any individual IE length field to a value that would cause the firmware's IE-walking loop to read past the frame boundary; a parser that iterates by consuming 'type + length + value' bytes from the IE chain would simply encounter the extra bytes as a large but structurally inert blob and stop at the end of the buffer. Fourth, assoc_request frames are state-gated: the target AP may silently discard Association Requests from a station that has not completed a valid Open System authentication exchange on that BSSID, meaning the association handler may never have executed against any of the 2716 assoc_request frames. The mutation set as designed therefore leaves the highest-risk parsing surfaces (beacon IE chain, RSN suite-count walks, truncated-IE edge cases) completely unreached.

## Findings
- [info] campaign/no_crash: All 7773 frames returned alive=1. The target survived every exercised mutation across assoc_request, authentication, and probe_request families without a single crash or loss of liveness.
- [anomaly] coverage/beacon_absent: The beacon frame family (subtype 8) was never included in the corpus despite being defined in the spec notes. The AP's IE-parsing path for beacon frames (SSID, TIM, RSN, DS Parameter Set, Country, Extended Supported Rates) is completely untested and represents the largest unexercised attack surface.
- [anomaly] coverage/corpus_is_20_frames_repeated: The per-frame log shows the same 20 unique frames (idx 0-19) repeated identically approximately 389 times each to reach 7773 total. Budget was entirely consumed on repetition of a fixed seed set; no coverage diversity was added after the first pass through the 20 frames.
- [anomaly] coverage/ie_truncation_mutation_absent: No exercised mutation crafts an IE whose declared length field exceeds the remaining bytes in the frame body. Truncated-IE parsing (where the firmware reads past frame end following a large IE length byte) is a classic out-of-bounds-read vector that is entirely absent from the current mutation set.
- [anomaly] coverage/rsn_ie_structure_unexercised: All assoc_request mutations target either fixed fields (assoc_cap_reserved, assoc_listen_zero, assoc_listen_max) or coarse structural patterns (dup_ie, missing_mandatory, oversized_value). No mutation specifically corrupts the RSN IE body: mismatched Pairwise Suite Count, mismatched AKM Count, or a truncated suite list that causes an off-by-one walk of the IE.
- [info] probe_request/oversized_value: probe_request/oversized_value (len=297, +247 bytes over baseline of 50) survived all replays. The target's probe-handling path handles bulk IE payload without crashing.
- [info] authentication/oversized_value: authentication/oversized_value (len=287) survived all replays. Open System authentication has no defined IEs; the extra bytes likely sit past the 6-byte fixed field and are discarded without being parsed, which explains why oversizing had no effect here.
- [info] assoc_request/oversized_value: assoc_request/oversized_value (len=327) survived all replays. Without a complementary truncated-IE variant the oversized body is structurally valid padding that a well-written IE walker skips cleanly.

## Next plan
{
  "focus_frames": [
    "beacon",
    "assoc_request",
    "authentication"
  ],
  "focus_mutations": [
    "ie_truncated_length",
    "ie_length_overflow",
    "rsn_suite_count_mismatch",
    "beacon_tim_corrupt",
    "beacon_ds_channel_oor",
    "beacon_country_truncated",
    "challenge_text_in_open_auth",
    "oversized_value"
  ],
  "drop_frames": [
    "probe_request"
  ],
  "rationale": "beacon must be added immediately \u2014 it is the largest unexercised family and the AP's IE parser for management frames is most consistently reachable via beacon injection regardless of association state. Recommended beacon mutations: ie_truncated_length (set SSID IE length = 0xFF so the IE walk reads past frame end), ie_length_overflow (set RSN IE length = 0xFF), beacon_tim_corrupt (DTIM Period = 0, Bitmap Control = 0xFF, partial bitmap length mismatch), beacon_ds_channel_oor (DS Parameter Set channel = 0x00 or 0xFF), beacon_country_truncated (Country IE length = 1, missing regulatory triplets). assoc_request should stay but shift to rsn_suite_count_mismatch (Pairwise Count claims 3 suites, only 1 suite present in IE body) and ie_truncated_length applied to the RSN IE specifically; these target the counter-driven loops that are distinct from the bulk-length checks that oversized_value already exercised. authentication should include challenge_text_in_open_auth (append IE 16 to an Open System algo=0 frame, which is undefined and may confuse length-driven parsers). probe_request is dropped: an AP in infrastructure mode does not crash from malformed Probe Requests in practice \u2014 1556 frames across all mutations confirmed survival \u2014 and the probe path is structurally simpler than beacon or association paths. Eliminating probe_request frees the full frame budget for beacon (which has zero prior coverage) and deeper assoc_request mutations. The corpus generator must also ensure each unique frame appears only once per campaign run to stop wasting budget on repetition of already-surviving seeds."
}
